                        cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pyrite FeS2 for high-rate and long-life rechargeable sodium batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hu, Zhe; Zhu, Zhiqiang; Cheng, Fangyi; Zhang, Kai; Wang, Jianbin; Chen, Chengcheng; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1309-1316</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">It is desirable to develop electrode materials for advanced rechargeable batteries with low cost, long life, and high-rate capability.  Pyrite FeS2, as an easily obtained natural mineral, has been already commercialized in primary lithium batteries, but encountered problems in rechargeable batteries with carbonate-based electrolytes due to the limited cycle life caused by the conversion-type reaction (FeS2 + 4M → Fe + 2M2S (M = Li or Na)).  Herein, we demonstrate that FeS2 microspheres can be applied in room-temp. rechargeable sodium batteries with only the intercalation reaction by simultaneously selecting a compatible NaSO3CF3/diglyme electrolyte and tuning the cut-off voltage to 0.8 V.  A surprisingly high-rate capability (170 mA h g-1 at 20 A g-1) and unprecedented long-term cyclability (∼90% capacity retention for 20 000 cycles) has been obtained.  We suggest that a stable elec. conductive layer-structured NaxFeS2 was formed during cycling, which enables the highly reversible sodium intercalation and deintercalation.  Moreover, 18650-type sodium batteries were constructed exhibiting a high capacity of ∼4200 mA h (corresponding to 126 W h kg-1 and 382 W h L-1) and a capacity retention of 97% after an initial 200 cycles at 4 A during charge-discharge.  This shows that the prodn. of rechargeable sodium batteries with FeS2 microspheres is viable for com. utilization.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrFxqeM-EGKh7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg6yuEl30E_wA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhs1arsL0%253D&amp;md5=25c3d019d88687effcc5109727ee9bce</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1016/j.jallcom.2006.02.113"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, T.         </div><div class="casAbstract">To develop the battery with low cost and high energy d., Na/FeS2 battery was prepd. using FeS2 powder synthesized by mech. alloying.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pyrite (FeS2) nanocrystals as inexpensive high-performance lithium-ion cathode and sodium-ion anode materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Walter, Marc; Zund, Tanja; Kovalenko, Maksym V.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">20</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">9158-9163</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In light of the impeding depletion of fossil fuels and necessity to lower carbon dioxide emissions, economically viable high-performance batteries are urgently needed for numerous applications ranging from elec. cars to stationary large-scale electricity storage.  Due to its low raw material cost, non-toxicity and potentially high charge-storage capacity pyrite (FeS2) is a highly promising material for such next-generation batteries.  In this work we present the electrochem. performance of FeS2 nanocrystals (NCs) as lithium-ion and sodium-ion storage materials.  First, we show that nanoscopic FeS2 is a promising lithium-ion cathode material, delivering a capacity of 715 mA h g-1 and av. energy d. of 1237 Wh kg-1 for 100 cycles, twice higher than for commonly used LiCoO2 cathodes.  Then we demonstrate, for the first time, that FeS2 NCs can serve as highly reversible sodium-ion anode material with long cycling life.  As sodium-ion anode material, FeS2 NCs provide capacities above 500 mA h g-1 for 400 cycles at a current rate of 1000 mA g-1.  In all our tests and control expts., the performance of chem. synthesized nanoscale FeS2 clearly surpasses bulk FeS2 as well as large no. of other nanostructured metal sulfides.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpJgqPrpm-HGbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljYsdlrGrvWRA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXntFSqtLg%253D&amp;md5=642ba0e3ef151768c60da79af8485f1f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA00623F"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, S.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Primary Li/FeS2 batteries have been commercialized and rechargeable Li-alloy/FeS2 batteries have been successfully operated at 375-500° by employing LiCl-based molten electrolytes.  However, non-aq. electrolyte rechargeable Li/FeS2 batteries have not yet been fulfilled due to poor reversibility and rapid capacity fading.  The redox mechanism of FeS2 in non-aq. electrolytes at ambient temp. is poorly understood and is still debated.  In this mini-review, the exptl. observations reported previously are analyzed and a suitable mechanism that can explain all of the phenomena obsd. from the non-aq. electrolyte Li/FeS2 and Na/FeS2 batteries is proposed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpveI6h_jvXILVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljYsdlrGrvWRA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXjsFWmsbo%253D&amp;md5=052d95e2191ec38efb8780cbbac0cce4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2007.06.093"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, T.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Discharge/charge reaction mechanism of a pyrite-type FeS2 cathode for sodium secondary batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kitajou, Ayuko; Yamaguchi, Junpei; Hara, Satoshi; Okada, Shigeto</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The structure changes of FeS2 during discharge/charge process were investigated by x-ray diffraction, XPS and synchrotron-based x-ray adsorption near the edge structure (XANES).  Although the cyclability of the FeS2/Na battery is poor, FeS2/Na battery has a large first discharge capacity of 758 mA-h/g.  It corresponds to 85% of the theor. capacity based on the 4.0 Na reaction per FeS2 (893 mA-h/g).  Based on the Fe K-edge XANES spectra of discharged FeS2 pellets, there were no clear traces of iron valence change.  However, the clear S K-edge jump shifted to lower energy with increasing Na content in FeS2.  This is because the binding energy of S 1s electrons decrease as the oxidn. no. of S decreases, suggesting that the charge neutrality of the cathode after 2.0 Na discharge is kept by an S valence change from (S-S)2- to S2-.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The use is demonstrated of FeSe2 as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries. The FeSe2 anode also exhibits long-term cyclic stability (372 mA h g-1 with capacity retention of 89.0% after 2000 cycles at 1 A g-1 ) and excellent high-rate performance 388 mA h g-1 at 10 C, 337 mA h g-1 at 20 C, 226 mA h g-1 at 50 C, where 1 C = 0.5 A g-1. Furthermore, the FeSe2 anode is coupled with an excessive Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode (the capacity of the Na3V2(PO4)3 is 1.5-2 times more than that of FeSe2) to fabricate a full cell, which exhibits a discharge capacity of 366 mA h g-1 based on the mass of FeSe2 with an av. output voltage of about 1.7 V at 1 A g-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqNZQmIWuA02rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljF4Ki0ZSk4Dw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXmslens7Y%253D&amp;md5=0ecc7e52e3b809d3dadbf828186e0859</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201200267"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yersak, T.                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon-Encapsulated Pyrite as Stable and Earth-Abundant High Energy Cathode Material for Rechargeable Lithium Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Jun; Wen, Yuren; Wang, Yi; van Aken, Peter A.; Maier, Joachim; Yu, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Porous pyrite nano-octahedra encapsulated by uniform carbon nanocages were prepd. via a facile self-sacrificing template route to serve as an electroactive cathode material.  Due to the shortened Li+ diffusion length, high contact surface area, good electronic cond. and superior structure stability of carbon-encapsulated pyrite, the as-obtained FeS2@C porous nano-octahedra exhibit superior rate capability (a reversible capability of 439, 340 and 256 mA h g-1 at 1, 2.5 and 5C, resp.) and stable cycling performance (approx. 10 % capacity loss after cycles at 0.5C with a capacity retention of 495 mA h g-1).                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">3D MoS2-Graphene Microspheres Consisting of Multiple Nanospheres with Superior Sodium Ion Storage Properties</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Choi, Seung Ho; Ko, You Na; Lee, Jung-Kul; Kang, Yun Chan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel anode material for sodium-ion batteries consisting of 3D graphene microspheres divided into several tens of uniform nanospheres coated with few-layered MoS2 by a one-pot spray pyrolysis process is prepd.  The first discharge/charge capacities of the composite microspheres are 797 and 573 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 0.2 A g-1.  The 600th discharge capacity of the composite microspheres at a c.d. of 1.5 A g-1 is 322 mA h g-1.  The Coulombic efficiency during the 600 cycles is as high as 99.98%.  The outstanding Na ion storage properties of the 3D MoS2-graphene composite microspheres may be attributed to the reduced stacking of the MoS2 layers and to the 3D structure of the porous graphene microspheres.  The reduced stacking of the MoS2 layers relaxes the strain and lowers the barrier for Na+ insertion.  The empty nanospheres of the graphene offer voids for vol. expansion and pathways for fast electron transfer during repeated cycling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp5MXJGPkuEhLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljF4Ki0ZSk4Dw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXkvVSitbk%253D&amp;md5=18c752a0885c5236fc4aefe504f5d301</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1038/srep12571"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sahu, T.                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Exfoliated MoS2 Sheets and Reduced Graphene Oxide-An Excellent and Fast Anode for Sodium-ion Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sahu, Tuhin Subhra; Mitra, Sagar</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Scientific Reports</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Three dimensional (3D) MoS2 nanoflowers are successfully synthesized by hydrothermal method.  Further, a composite of as prepd. MoS2 nanoflowers and rGO is constructed by simple ultrasonic exfoliation technique.  The crystallog. and morphol. studies have been carried out by XRD, FE-SEM, TEM, HR-TEM and EDS etc.  Here, XRD study revealed, a composite of exfoliated MoS2 with expanded spacing of (002) crystal plane and rGO can be prepd. by simple 40 min of ultrasonic treatment.  While, FE-SEM and TEM studies depict, individual MoS2 nanoflowers with an av. diam. of 200 nm are uniformly distributed throughout the rGO surface.  When tested as sodium-ion batteries anode material by applying two different potential windows, the composite demonstrates a high reversible specific capacity of 575 mAhg-1 at 100 mAg-1 in between 0.01 V-2.6 V and 218 mAhg-1 at 50 mAg-1 when discharged in a potential range of 0.4 V-2.6 V.  As per our concern, the results are one of the best obtained as compared to the earlier published one on MoS2 based SIB anode material and more importantly this material shows such an excellent reversible Na-storage capacity and good cycling stability without addn. of any expensive additive stabilizer, like fluoroethylene carbonate (FEC), in comparison to those in current literature.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrdZCsfc4XUF7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljF4Ki0ZSk4Dw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MoS2-reduced graphene oxide composites via microwave assisted synthesis for sodium ion battery anode with improved capacity and cycling performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Qin, Wei; Chen, Taiqiang; Pan, Likun; Niu, Lengyuan; Hu, Bingwen; Li, Dongsheng; Li, Jinliang; Sun, Zhuo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">MoS2-reduced graphene oxide (RGO) composites were synthesized via a facile microwave assisted redn. of graphene oxide in MoS2 precursor soln. and subsequent annealing in N2/H2 atmosphere at 800° for 2 h. The MoS2-RGO composites with different RGO loadings were applied as anode materials of Na ion batteries (SIBs) and they exhibit a max. reversible specific capacity of ∼305 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1 after 50 cycles and excellent rate performance.                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sandwich-like cobalt sulfide-graphene composite - an anode material with excellent electrochemical performance for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Qian; Liu, Li; Guo, Guoxiong; Yan, Zichao; Tan, Jinli; Huang, Zhifeng; Chen, Xiaoying; Wang, Xianyou</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">RSC Advances</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Recently, sodium-ion batteries have been considered alternatives to lithium-ion batteries.  However, the poor cycling performance and unsatisfactory rate capability of existing anodes hinder the development of sodium-ion batteries.  Here we fabricate a sandwich-like cobalt sulfide-reduced graphene oxide (CoS/rGO) composite using a hydrothermal method as the anode material for sodium ion batteries.  According to the SEM anal., CoS nanoparticles anchor on both sides of the reduced graphene oxide nanosheets in such a way that the nanoporous structure with a large amt. of void spaces can be prepd.  And the cycling performance of the sandwich-like CoS/rGO composite is drastically enhanced compared with that of the bare CoS nanoparticles.  After 100 cycles, the discharge capacity of CoS/rGO still remains at 230 mA h g-1, while the specific capacity of the bare CoS nanoparticles at the first cycle is 601 mA h g-1, dropping rapidly to 68 mA h g-1 after only 40 cycles.  Furthermore, CoS/rGO gives an excellent rate capability even up to a large current of 2 A g-1.  It is noted that the synergistic effect between CoS and graphene can contribute to the improved electrochem. performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq-eSWKiUzXs7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljQI5UYCVSw4A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtlCktrvM&amp;md5=bc12554a9476281fdc7dd3fc7c7973eb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA00621J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Du, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dai, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bao, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> porous Nanosheets Embedded in Graphene Sheets as High-Performance Anode Materials for Lithium and Sodium Storage</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hybrid of Co3Sn2@Co nanoparticles and nitrogen-doped graphene as a lithium ion battery anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Mahmood, Nasir; Zhang, Chenzhen; Liu, Fei; Zhu, Jinghan; Hou, Yanglong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A facile strategy was designed for the fabrication of hybrid of Co3Sn2@Co nanoparticles (NPs) and nitrogen-doped graphene (NG) sheets through a hydrothermal synthesis, followed by annealing process.  Core-shell architecture of Co3Sn2@Co pin on NG is designed for the dual encapsulation of Co3Sn2 with adaptable ensembles of Co and NG to address the structural and interfacial stability concerns facing tin-based anodes.  In the resulted unique architecture of Co3Sn2@Co-NG hybrid, the sealed cobalt cover prevents the direct exposer of Sn with electrolyte because of encapsulated structure and keeps the structural and interfacial integrity of Co3Sn2.  However, the elastically strong, flexible and conductive NG overcoat accommodates the vol. changes and therefore brings the structural and elec. stabilization of Co3Sn2@Co NPs.  As a result, Co3Sn2@Co-NG hybrid exhibits extraordinary reversible capacity of 1615 mAh/g at 250 mA/g after 100 cycles with excellent capacity retention of 102%.  The hybrid bears superior rate capability with reversible capacity of 793.9 mAh/g at 2500 mA/g and Coulombic efficiency nearly 100%.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpt6M90oS-qhbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljQI5UYCVSw4A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhs1WltbjO&amp;md5=8fc9058f3accd2482d74437376ccbe19</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xie, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, S.-Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, X.-F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zheng, Y.-X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Song, W.-T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cao, G.-S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, T.-J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, X.-B.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nanocrystal-SnO<sub>2</sub>-Loaded Graphene with Improved Li-Storage Properties Prepared by a Facile One-Pot Hydrothermal Route</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Int. J. Electrochem.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nanocrystal-SnO2-loaded graphene with improved Li-storage properties prepared by a facile one-pot hydrothermal route</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xie, Jian; Liu, Shuang-Yu; Chen, Xue-Fei; Zheng, Yun-Xiao; Song, Wen-Tao; Cao, Gao-Shao; Zhu, Tie-Jun; Zhao, Xin-Bing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">International Journal of Electrochemical Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2011</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5539-5549</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Electrochemical Science Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nanocrystal-SnO2-loaded graphene was synthesized by a facile in situ one-pot hydrothermal route.  The effects of tin sources (Sn2+ or Sn4+) and graphene on the morphol. and electrochem. properties of SnO2 have been investigated.  It was found that the graphite oxide plays a crit. role in the oxidn. of Sn2+ to Sn4+, and that SnO instead of SnO2 forms without adding the graphite oxide.  SnO2 exhibits a smaller size (below 10 nm) and a more homogeneous dispersion on graphene using Sn2+ as the precursor compared with the case using Sn4+ as the precursor.  The electrochem. tests showed that the SnO2-graphene nanocomposites exhibit obvious improved electrochem. properties compared to bare SnO2 due to the buffering, confining and conducting effects of the introduced graphene.  We also found that the nanocomposite using Sn2+ as the precursor shows a better cycling stability than that using Sn4+ as the precursor.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqG7jM78BhPArVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgO8QiR3g9LnQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXhsFagtLjL&amp;md5=9ff520b030214893ddda70772ba67625</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, S.-Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xie, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pan, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, C.-Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cao, G.-S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, T.-J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, X.-B.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Graphene Anchored with Nanocrystal Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> with Improved Electrochemical Li-Storage Properties</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Int.                         cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Significant enhancement of blue emission and electrical conductivity of N-doped graphene</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Van Khai, Tran; Na, Han Gil; Kwak, Dong Sub; Kwon, Yong Jung; Ham, Heon; Shim, Kwang Bo; Kim, Hyoun Woo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">22</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">34</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">17992-18003</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nitrogen (N)-doped graphene with different at. percentages (2.3-4.7 at%) of N has been synthesized by thermal annealing of reduced graphene oxide (RGO) in ammonia gas for different times.  The effects of annealing time on the structure, elec. and optical properties of N-doped graphene have been systematically investigated by using various anal. techniques.  XPS, FTIR, Raman, and XRD studies show that there is a gradual structural change in N-doped graphene sheets with increasing annealing time, resulting from the increase of carbon and simultaneous decrease of oxygen and N contents.  High resoln. N1s spectra reveal that the pyridine-N and pyrrolic-N contents decrease with increasing annealing time, whereas the amt. of quaternary-N increases.  Importantly, it has been found that the annealing time caused significant changes in both the elec. and the optical properties of N-doped graphene.  The elec. resistance of N-doped graphene is greatly reduced compared to that of GO and RGO, and found to further decrease with increasing annealing time, possibly due to the increase of sp2 carbon networks and decrease of oxygen content as well as defects assocd. with the incorporation of N.  The room-temp. photoluminescence (PL) properties of graphene oxide (GO), RGO and N-doped graphene were systematically studied with regard to the annealing time.  The results showed that the PL spectrum of GO exhibits a peak emission max. at around 700 nm, while that of RGO is found to be strongly blue-shifted with two distinct emission peaks: green emission at 485-500 nm and blue emission at 420-428 nm.  For N-doped graphene samples, the blue emission intensity could significantly be enhanced by controlling the annealing time, which leads to a promising blue and green light-emitting material with controllable optical properties.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp2as2FUiWeLrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgO8QiR3g9LnQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhtFGks7%252FM&amp;md5=b55cb48dfacc9d67b94e84dc7fe47842</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2014.03.118"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">He, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Phosphorus-Doped Reduced Graphene Oxide as an Electrocatalyst Counter Electrode in Dye-Sensitized Solar Cells</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Phosphorus-doped reduced graphene oxide as an electrocatalyst counter electrode in dye-sensitized solar cells</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Zegao; Li, Pingjian; Chen, Yuanfu; He, Jiarui; Liu, Jingbo; Zhang, Wanli; Li, Yanrong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

                        cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nitrogen and sulfur dual-doped reduced graphene oxide: synergistic effect of dopants towards oxygen redn. reaction</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Bag, Sourav; Mondal, Bodhisatwa; Das, Ashok Kumar; Raj, C. Retna</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">We describe a facile single-step non-hydrothermal chem. route for the synthesis of N and S dual-doped reduced graphene oxide (SN-rGO) and the synergistic effect of N and S in oxygen redn. reaction (ORR).  The redn. of graphene oxide (GO) and dual doping of rGO are achieved in one-step with a single doping agent in ethylene glycol.  SN-rGO has pyridinic and pyrrolic nitrogen and thiophenic sulfur and it has N/C and S/C at. ratio of 0.12 and 0.08, resp.  The at. percentage of pyridinic N (66%) is significantly higher than pyrrolic N (34%).  The electrocatalytic performance of SN-rGO towards ORR is examd. in terms of onset potential, kinetic c.d., no. of electrons transferred, durability and methanol tolerance in alk. soln.  SN-rGO shows excellent electrocatalytic activity with an onset potential of -15 mV (Hg/HgO) and it tends promotes the four electron pathway.  The activity of SN-rGO is superior to that of rGO doped only with N and S (N-rGO and S-rGO) and undoped rGO.  The comparison of the ORR activity of SN-rGO with N-rGO and S-rGO indicates the synergistic effect of heteroatoms of SN-rGO in the electrocatalytic reaction.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion battery is playing an important role as a low-cost alternative power source to Li-ion battery.  Developing novel carbonaceous anode materials is highly demanded for high performance and environmental benignity.  We report, for the first time, the graphene sheets covalently bonded with sulfur atoms as Na-ion battery anode material with a large reversible capacity of 291 mA h g-1 and an outstanding rate capability with 127 and 83 mA h g-1 at 2.0 and 5.0 A g-1 (charging/discharging in 3.8 and 1 min, resp.), and a long cycling stability as well.  Both expt. and d. functional theory calcn. proves that the superior performance is mainly attributed to the unique nanoporous structure stemmed from the chem. S doping.  This material holds great promise in future application of low cost, high-performance Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoPVOvcWrCv4LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljLuy343y61hw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtVeis7vJ&amp;md5=8e2f26320815fe397f97730457191424</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2014.03.078"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ahn, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Song, H.                         cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Preferential c-Axis Orientation of Ultrathin SnS2 Nanoplates on Graphene as High-Performance Anode for Li-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Shuangyu; Lu, Xiang; Xie, Jian; Cao, Gaoshao; Zhu, Tiejun; Zhao, Xinbing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1588-1595</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A SnS2/graphene (SnS2/G) hybrid was synthesized by a facile 1-step solvothermal route using graphite oxide, Na sulfide, and SnCl4·5H2O as the starting materials.  The formation of SnS2 and the redn. of graphite oxide occur simultaneously.  Ultrathin SnS2 nanoplates with a lateral size of 5-10 nm are anchored on graphene nanosheets with a preferential (001) orientation, forming a unique plate-on-sheet structure.  The electrochem. tests showed that the nanohybrid exhibits a remarkably enhanced cycling stability and rate capability compared with bare SnS2.  The excellent electrochem. properties of SnS2/G could be ascribed to the in situ introduced graphene matrix which offers 2-dimensional conductive networks, disperses and immobilizes SnS2 nanoplates, buffers the vol. changes during cycling, and directs the growth of SnS2 nanoplates with a favorable orientation.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoUJzYXZ6hCDrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljLuy343y61hw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXivVyjtrw%253D&amp;md5=6c72775363e17058cd0e13649afbc220</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201404078"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xie, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ao, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Su, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, G.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">MoS<sub>2</sub>/Graphene Composite Anodes with Enhanced Performance for Sodium-Ion Batteries: The Role of the Two-Dimensional Heterointerface</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.                         cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MoS2/Graphene Composite Anodes with Enhanced Performance for Sodium-Ion Batteries: The Role of the Two-Dimensional Heterointerface</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xie, Xiuqiang; Ao, Zhimin; Su, Dawei; Zhang, Jinqiang; Wang, Guoxiu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">25</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1393-1403</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphene has been widely used as conformal nanobuilding blocks to improve the electrochem. performance of layered metal sulfides (MoS2, WS2, SnS, and SnS2) as anode materials for sodium-ion batteries.  However, it still lacks in-depth understanding of the synergistic effect between these layered sulfides and graphene, which contributes to the enhanced electroactivity for sodium-ion batteries.  Here, MoS2/reduced graphene oxide (RGO) nanocomposites with intimate two-dimensional heterointerfaces are prepd. by a facile one-pot hydrothermal method.  The heterointerfacial area can be effectively tuned by changing the ratio of MoS2 to RGO.  When used as anode materials for sodium-ion batteries, the synergistic effect contributing to the enhanced reversible capacity of MoS2/RGO nanocomposites is closely related with the heterointerfacial area.  The computational results demonstrate that Na prefers to be adsorbed on MoS2 in the MoS2/RGO heterostructure rather than intercalate into the MoS2/RGO heterointerface.  Interestingly, the MoS2/RGO heterointerfaces can significantly increase the electronic cond. of MoS2, store more Na ions, while maintaining the high diffusion mobility of Na atoms on MoS2 surface and high electron transfer efficiency from Na to MoS2.  It is expected that the efforts to establish the correlation between the two-dimensional heterointerface and the electrochem. sodium-ion storage performance offer fundamental understanding for the rational design of layered metal sulfides/graphene composites as high-performance electrode materials for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpB50PmkRDAvrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljLuy343y61hw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsVansbY%253D&amp;md5=3d82ce10422e6d348a48b628852d1b2b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref47'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit47" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201306314"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qu, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ma, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ji, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Meng, Y.                         cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Layered SnS2-reduced graphene oxide (RGO) composite - A high-capacity, high-rate, and long-cycle life sodium-ion battery anode material</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Qu, Baihua; Ma, Chuze; Ji, Ge; Xu, Chaohe; Xu, Jing; Meng, Ying Shirley; Wang, Taihong; Lee, Jim Yang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

                        cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Self-assembly of CoS2/graphene nanoarchitecture by a facile one-pot route and its improved electrochemical Li-storage properties</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xie, Jian; Liu, Shuangyu; Cao, Gaoshao; Zhu, Tiejun; Zhao, Xinbing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">49-56</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A CoS2/graphene nanoarchitecture was synthesized by a facile one-step hydrothermal route using graphite oxide, thioacetamide, and CoCl2·6H2O as the starting materials.                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sulfur-Doped Graphene as an Efficient Metal-free Cathode Catalyst for Oxygen Reduction</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Zhi; Yao, Zhen; Li, Guifa; Fang, Guoyong; Nie, Huagui; Liu, Zheng; Zhou, Xuemei; Chen, Xi'an; Huang, Shaoming</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">205-211</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Tailoring the electronic arrangement of graphene by doping is a practical strategy for producing significantly improved materials for the O-redn. reaction (ORR) in fuel cells (FCs).  Recent studies proved that the C materials doped with the elements, which have the larger (N) or smaller (P, B) electroneg. atoms than C such as N-doped C nanotubes (CNTs), P-doped graphite layers and B-doped CNTs, also showed pronounced catalytic activity.  Herein, the graphenes doped with the elements, which have the similar electronegativity with C such as S and Se, can also exhibit better catalytic activity than the com. Pt/C in alk. media, indicating that these doped graphenes hold great potential for a substitute for Pt-based catalysts in FCs.  The exptl. results are believed to be significant because they not only give further insight into the ORR mechanism of these metal-free doped C materials, but also open a way to fabricate other new low-cost NPMCs with high electrocatalytic activity by a simple, economical, and scalable approach for real FC applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqWQqbSkhy1lbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljWh-QBHNiMIw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXhs1OjtbrN&amp;md5=e5861429d3b9a9dbb423b3c96fd22c05</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref51'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit51" data-doi="10.1002/advs.201500195"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qie, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xiong, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zou, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sulfur-Doped Carbon with Enlarged Interlayer Distance as a High-Performance Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.                 10.1002/advs.201500195</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D2%26publication_year%3D2015%26journal%3DAdv.%2BScience%26author%3DL.%2BQie%26author%3DW.%2BChen%26author%3DX.%2BXiong%26author%3DC.%2BHu%26author%3DF.%2BZou%26author%3DP.%2BHu%26author%3DY.%2BHuang%26title%3DSulfur-Doped%2BCarbon%2Bwith%2BEnlarged%2BInterlayer%2BDistance%2Bas%2Ba%2BHigh-Performance%2BAnode%2BMaterial%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadvs.201500195&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.5b12148&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadvs.201500195&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable Li batteries have risen to prominence as key devices for green and sustainable energy development.  Mn- and Fe-based cathode materials, such as LiMn2O4 and LiFePO4, are used in large-scale batteries for elec. vehicles.  Mn and Fe are abundant elements in the Earth's crust, but Li is not.  In contrast to Li, Na is an attractive charge carrier from elemental abundance.  Recently, some layered materials, where Na can be electrochem. and reversibly extd./inserted, have been reported.  However, their reversible capacity is typically limited to 100 mA-h/g.  Herein, the authors report a new electrode material, P2-Na2/3[Fe1/2Mn1/2]O2, that delivers 190 mA-h/g of reversible capacity in Na cells with the electrochem. active Fe3+/Fe4+ redox.  These results will contribute to the development of rechargeable batteries from the earth-abundant elements operable at room temp.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoHU9moaXs6J7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lin4OFxX9cnPA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38Xmt1GqtL8%253D&amp;md5=519efcb60bb0a6fd4843546d51921eb7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1021/nl3016957"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cao, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xiao, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sushko, M.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Hollow carbon nanowires were prepd. by pyrolysis of a hollow polyaniline nanowire precursor.  The hollow carbon nanowires used as anode material for Na-ion batteries deliver a high reversible capacity of 251 mA-h/g and 82.2% capacity retention over 400 charge-discharge cycles between 1.2 and 0.01 V (vs. Na+/Na) at a const. current of 50 mA/g (0.2C).         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Energy prodn. and storage have become key issues concerning our welfare in daily life.  Present challenges for batteries are twofold.  In the first place, the increasing demand for powering systems of portable electronic devices and zero-emission vehicles stimulates research towards high energy and high voltage systems.  In the second place, low cost batteries are required in order to advance towards smart elec. grids that integrate discontinuous energy flow from renewable sources, optimizing the performance of clean energy sources.  Na-ion batteries can be the key for the second point, because of the huge availability of sodium, its low price and the similarity of both Li and Na insertion chemistries.  In spite of the lower energy d. and voltage of Na-ion based technologies, they can be focused on applications where the wt. and footprint requirement is less drastic, such as elec. grid storage.  Much work has to be done in the field of Na-ion in order to catch up with Li-ion technol.  Cathodic and anodic materials must be optimized, and new electrolytes will be the key point for Na-ion success.  This review will gather the up-to-date knowledge about Na-ion battery materials, with the aim of providing a wide view of the systems that have already been explored and a starting point for the new research on this battery technol.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoRYtxfVVW_sLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lin4OFxX9cnPA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XivFWnu7s%253D&amp;md5=72869139086b8ee9adec746418ff84b1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref7" class="rightTabRefNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit7" data-doi="10.1039/c3cp52125g"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Klein, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jache, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bhide, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Adelhelm, P.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Conversion Reactions for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Phys.                         rightTab-cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Conversion reactions for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Klein, Franziska; Jache, Birte; Bhide, Amrtha; Adelhelm, Philipp</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Chemistry Chemical Physics</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Research on Na-ion batteries is focused on finding suitable electrode materials that enable cell reactions of high energy densities combined with low cost.  Naturally, an assessment of potential electrode materials requires a rational comparison with the analog reaction in Li-ion batteries.  The authors discuss the broad range of different conversion reactions for Na-ion batteries based on their basic thermodn. properties and compare them with their Li analogs.  Capacities, voltages, energy densities and vol. expansions are summarized to sketch out the scope for future studies in this research field.  For a given conversion electrode material, replacing Li by Na leads to a const. shift in cell potential ΔEo(Li-Na) depending on the material class.  For chlorides ΔEo(Li-Na) is nearly zero.  The theor. energy densities of conversion reactions of Na with fluorides or chlorides as pos. electrode materials typically reach values between 700 W h kg-1 and 1000 W h kg-1.  Next to the thermodn. assessment, results on several conversion reactions between Cu compds. (CuS, CuO, CuCl, CuCl2) and Na are being discussed.  Reactions with CuS and CuO were chosen because these compds. are frequently studied for conversion reactions with Li.  Chlorides are interesting because of ΔEo(Li-Na) ≈ 0 V As a result of chloride soly. in the electrolyte, the conversion process proceeds at defined potentials under rather small kinetic limitations.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpvFdD49Ctj47Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhDobNgtktB7w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhsVWrtbrE&amp;md5=7135136abf30b3a83827d65de85c8f45</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref8" class="rightTabRefNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit8" data-doi="10.1039/C4CC09604E"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, W.                         rightTab-cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A New High-Energy Cathode for a Na-Ion Battery with Ultrahigh Stability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Park, Young-Uk; Seo, Dong-Hwa; Kwon, Hyung-Soon; Kim, Byoungkook; Kim, Jongsoon; Kim, Haegyeom; Kim, Inkyung; Yoo, Han-Ill; Kang, Kisuk</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Large-scale elec. energy storage is a key enabler for the use of renewable energy.  Recently, the room-temp. Na-ion battery has been re-highlighted as an alternative low-cost technol. for this application.  However, significant challenges such as energy d. and long-term stability must be addressed.  Herein, we introduce a novel cathode material, Na1.5VPO4.8F0.7, for Na-ion batteries.  This new material provides an energy d. of ∼600 Wh kg-1, the highest value among cathodes, originating from both the multielectron redox reaction (1.2 e- per formula unit) and the high potential (∼3.8 V vs Na+/Na) of the tailored vanadium redox couple (V3.8+/V5+).  Furthermore, an outstanding cycle life (∼95% capacity retention for 100 cycles and ∼84% for extended 500 cycles) could be achieved, which we attribute to the small vol. change (2.9%) upon cycling, the smallest vol. change among known Na intercalation cathodes.  The open crystal framework with two-dimensional Na diffusional pathways leads to low activation barriers for Na diffusion, enabling excellent rate capability.  We believe that this new material can bring the low-cost room-temp. Na-ion battery a step closer to a sustainable large-scale energy storage system.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpMgFNhDwY4a7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhDobNgtktB7w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXht1ymtLjL&amp;md5=dfcdb36e705456054d32760606a6f305</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref10" class="rightTabRefNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit10" data-doi="10.1039/C5NR02064F"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shang, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lu, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jiao, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">NaV<sub>3</sub>O<sub>8</sub> Nanosheet@Polypyrrole Core-Shell Composites with Good Electrochemical Performance as Cathodes for Na-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nanoscale</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">7</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">9261</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">9267</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Novel NaV3O8 nanosheet@polypyrrole core-shell composites have been successfully prepd. for the first time via a chem. oxidative polymn. method.  Based on the morphol. and microstructural characterization, it was found that polypyrrole (PPy) was uniformly wrapped on the surfaces of the NaV3O8 nanosheets.  When used as a cathode for Na-ion batteries, the as-synthesized NaV3O8@10% PPy composite showed significantly improved cycling performance (with a discharge capacity of 99 mA h g-1 after 60 cycles at 80 mA g-1) and better rate capacity (with a discharge capacity of 63 mA h g-1 at a high c.d. of 640 mA g-1) than pristine NaV3O8 nanosheets.  The greatly enhanced performance benefits from the unique core-shell structure, where the PPy coating not only prevents the pulverization and aggregation of the lamellar NaV3O8 nanosheets during cycling, which can improve the cycling stability, but also enhances the elec. cond. of the composite, which can facilitate Na+ ion diffusion.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoIpRpX1Dm6s7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhDobNgtktB7w"> &gt;&gt; Structural and morphol. characterizations demonstrate that ultrasmall SnS2 nanoplates (with a typical size of 20-50 nm) composed of 2-5 layers are homogeneously decorated on the surface of graphene, while the hybrid structure self-assembles into a three-dimensional (3D) network architecture. The excellent electrochem. performance is attributed to the synergetic effects between the ultrasmall SnS2 and the highly conductive graphene network.                         rightTab-cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Expanded graphite as superior anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wen, Yang; He, Kai; Zhu, Yujie; Han, Fudong; Xu, Yunhua; Matsuda, Isamu; Ishii, Yoshitaka; Cumings, John; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphite, as the most common anode for com. Li-ion batteries, has been reported to have a very low capacity when used as a Na-ion battery anode.  It is well known that electrochem. insertion of Na+ into graphite is significantly hindered by the insufficient interlayer spacing.  Here we report expanded graphite as a Na-ion battery anode.  Prepd. through a process of oxidn. and partial redn. on graphite, expanded graphite has an enlarged interlayer lattice distance of 4.3 Å yet retains an analogous long-range-ordered layered structure to graphite.  In situ transmission electron microscopy has demonstrated that the Na-ion can be reversibly inserted into and extd. from expanded graphite.  Galvanostatic studies show that expanded graphite can deliver a high reversible capacity of 284 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 20 mA g-1, maintain a capacity of 184 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1, and retain 73.92% of its capacity after 2,000 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrFEZ8wJYk1irVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljIfiNPtVtByg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXksVeqs7g%253D&amp;md5=e4bc2edac8d22121e7986e165b7df007</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref14" class="rightTabRefNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit14" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2012.12.072"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qie, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yuan, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Functionalized N-Doped Interconnected Carbon Nanofibers as an Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Storage with Excellent Performance</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Carbon</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">55</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">328</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">334</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The electrochem. properties of Na/TiS2 cells fabricated using Na anodes and TiS2 cathodes and 1M sodium trifluoromethanesulfonate in tetraethylene glycol di-Me ether liq. electrolyte have been investigated.  The discharge curve has two plateau regions of 2.1 V and 1.6 V.  The loss of discharge capacity appeared mainly in the upper plateau region (2.0-2.6 V) and the discharge capacity in the low plateau region (0.8-2.0 V) does not decrease and is consistent during 40 cycles.  The discharge process between Na and TiS2 has a complex reaction mechanism, the intercalation at the upper plateau region and the conversion at the low plateau region.  Because, a distorted TiS2 phase appeared in the upper plateau, a new phase of NaxTiS2 was obsd. in the lower plateau, and the NaxTiS2 phase disappeared after full discharge as obsd. by x-ray diffraction and TEM.  The decrease of discharge capacity during cycling is a result of the formation of NaxTiS2 phase in the cathode after full charging and this phase accumulates by repeated cycling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp4Oxeuj1-6xLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljIfiNPtVtByg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhvFOiur8%253D&amp;md5=7f8304e44014d69c22b1c29f1ff87554</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref19" class="rightTabRefNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit19" data-doi="10.1039/c3cc41934g"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yue, J.                         rightTab-cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pyrite FeS2 for high-rate and long-life rechargeable sodium batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hu, Zhe; Zhu, Zhiqiang; Cheng, Fangyi; Zhang, Kai; Wang, Jianbin; Chen, Chengcheng; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1309-1316</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">It is desirable to develop electrode materials for advanced rechargeable batteries with low cost, long life, and high-rate capability.  Pyrite FeS2, as an easily obtained natural mineral, has been already commercialized in primary lithium batteries, but encountered problems in rechargeable batteries with carbonate-based electrolytes due to the limited cycle life caused by the conversion-type reaction (FeS2 + 4M → Fe + 2M2S (M = Li or Na)).  Herein, we demonstrate that FeS2 microspheres can be applied in room-temp. rechargeable sodium batteries with only the intercalation reaction by simultaneously selecting a compatible NaSO3CF3/diglyme electrolyte and tuning the cut-off voltage to 0.8 V.  A surprisingly high-rate capability (170 mA h g-1 at 20 A g-1) and unprecedented long-term cyclability (∼90% capacity retention for 20 000 cycles) has been obtained.  We suggest that a stable elec. conductive layer-structured NaxFeS2 was formed during cycling, which enables the highly reversible sodium intercalation and deintercalation.  Moreover, 18650-type sodium batteries were constructed exhibiting a high capacity of ∼4200 mA h (corresponding to 126 W h kg-1 and 382 W h L-1) and a capacity retention of 97% after an initial 200 cycles at 4 A during charge-discharge.  This shows that the prodn. of rechargeable sodium batteries with FeS2 microspheres is viable for com. utilization.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrFxqeM-EGKh7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lisXXS_4tTo_Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhs1arsL0%253D&amp;md5=25c3d019d88687effcc5109727ee9bce</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref22" class="rightTabRefNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit22" data-doi="10.1016/j.jallcom.2006.02.113"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, T.         </div><div class="casAbstract">In light of the impeding depletion of fossil fuels and necessity to lower carbon dioxide emissions, economically viable high-performance batteries are urgently needed for numerous applications ranging from elec. cars to stationary large-scale electricity storage.  Due to its low raw material cost, non-toxicity and potentially high charge-storage capacity pyrite (FeS2) is a highly promising material for such next-generation batteries.  In this work we present the electrochem. performance of FeS2 nanocrystals (NCs) as lithium-ion and sodium-ion storage materials.  First, we show that nanoscopic FeS2 is a promising lithium-ion cathode material, delivering a capacity of 715 mA h g-1 and av. energy d. of 1237 Wh kg-1 for 100 cycles, twice higher than for commonly used LiCoO2 cathodes.  Then we demonstrate, for the first time, that FeS2 NCs can serve as highly reversible sodium-ion anode material with long cycling life.  As sodium-ion anode material, FeS2 NCs provide capacities above 500 mA h g-1 for 400 cycles at a current rate of 1000 mA g-1.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The use is demonstrated of FeSe2 as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries.  The FeSe2 microspheres assembled by nanooctahedra display a high tapping d. of 1.85 g cm-3 and a discharge capacity of 447 mA h g-1 at 0.1 A g-1.  The FeSe2 anode also exhibits long-term cyclic stability (372 mA h g-1 with capacity retention of 89.0% after 2000 cycles at 1 A g-1 ) and excellent high-rate performance 388 mA h g-1 at 10 C, 337 mA h g-1 at 20 C, 226 mA h g-1 at 50 C, where 1 C = 0.5 A g-1. Furthermore, the FeSe2 anode is coupled with an excessive Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode (the capacity of the Na3V2(PO4)3 is 1.5-2 times more than that of FeSe2) to fabricate a full cell, which exhibits a discharge capacity of 366 mA h g-1 based on the mass of FeSe2 with an av. output voltage of about 1.7 V at 1 A g-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqNZQmIWuA02rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhL06NMdqarDg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXmslens7Y%253D&amp;md5=0ecc7e52e3b809d3dadbf828186e0859</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref30" class="rightTabRefNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit30" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201200267"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yersak, T.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel anode material for sodium-ion batteries consisting of 3D graphene microspheres divided into several tens of uniform nanospheres coated with few-layered MoS2 by a one-pot spray pyrolysis process is prepd.  The first discharge/charge capacities of the composite microspheres are 797 and 573 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 0.2 A g-1.  The 600th discharge capacity of the composite microspheres at a c.d. of 1.5 A g-1 is 322 mA h g-1.  The Coulombic efficiency during the 600 cycles is as high as 99.98%.  The outstanding Na ion storage properties of the 3D MoS2-graphene composite microspheres may be attributed to the reduced stacking of the MoS2 layers and to the 3D structure of the porous graphene microspheres.  The reduced stacking of the MoS2 layers relaxes the strain and lowers the barrier for Na+ insertion.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Recently, sodium-ion batteries have been considered alternatives to lithium-ion batteries.  However, the poor cycling performance and unsatisfactory rate capability of existing anodes hinder the development of sodium-ion batteries.  Here we fabricate a sandwich-like cobalt sulfide-reduced graphene oxide (CoS/rGO) composite using a hydrothermal method as the anode material for sodium ion batteries.  According to the SEM anal., CoS nanoparticles anchor on both sides of the reduced graphene oxide nanosheets in such a way that the nanoporous structure with a large amt. of void spaces can be prepd.  And the cycling performance of the sandwich-like CoS/rGO composite is drastically enhanced compared with that of the bare CoS nanoparticles.  After 100 cycles, the discharge capacity of CoS/rGO still remains at 230 mA h g-1, while the specific capacity of the bare CoS nanoparticles at the first cycle is 601 mA h g-1, dropping rapidly to 68 mA h g-1 after only 40 cycles.  Furthermore, CoS/rGO gives an excellent rate capability even up to a large current of 2 A g-1.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Nanocrystal-SnO2-loaded graphene was synthesized by a facile in situ one-pot hydrothermal route.  The effects of tin sources (Sn2+ or Sn4+) and graphene on the morphol. and electrochem. properties of SnO2 have been investigated.  It was found that the graphite oxide plays a crit. role in the oxidn. of Sn2+ to Sn4+, and that SnO instead of SnO2 forms without adding the graphite oxide.                         rightTab-cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Significant enhancement of blue emission and electrical conductivity of N-doped graphene</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Van Khai, Tran; Na, Han Gil; Kwak, Dong Sub; Kwon, Yong Jung; Ham, Heon; Shim, Kwang Bo; Kim, Hyoun Woo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">22</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nitrogen (N)-doped graphene with different at. percentages (2.3-4.7 at%) of N has been synthesized by thermal annealing of reduced graphene oxide (RGO) in ammonia gas for different times.  The effects of annealing time on the structure, elec. and optical properties of N-doped graphene have been systematically investigated by using various anal. techniques.  XPS, FTIR, Raman, and XRD studies show that there is a gradual structural change in N-doped graphene sheets with increasing annealing time, resulting from the increase of carbon and simultaneous decrease of oxygen and N contents.  High resoln. N1s spectra reveal that the pyridine-N and pyrrolic-N contents decrease with increasing annealing time, whereas the amt. of quaternary-N increases.  Importantly, it has been found that the annealing time caused significant changes in both the elec. and the optical properties of N-doped graphene.  The elec. resistance of N-doped graphene is greatly reduced compared to that of GO and RGO, and found to further decrease with increasing annealing time, possibly due to the increase of sp2 carbon networks and decrease of oxygen content as well as defects assocd. with the incorporation of N.  The room-temp. photoluminescence (PL) properties of graphene oxide (GO), RGO and N-doped graphene were systematically studied with regard to the annealing time.  The results showed that the PL spectrum of GO exhibits a peak emission max. at around 700 nm, while that of RGO is found to be strongly blue-shifted with two distinct emission peaks: green emission at 485-500 nm and blue emission at 420-428 nm.  For N-doped graphene samples, the blue emission intensity could significantly be enhanced by controlling the annealing time, which leads to a promising blue and green light-emitting material with controllable optical properties.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp2as2FUiWeLrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgx5rUH5-K1pA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhtFGks7%252FM&amp;md5=b55cb48dfacc9d67b94e84dc7fe47842</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref41" class="rightTabRefNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit41" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2014.03.118"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">He, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Phosphorus-Doped Reduced Graphene Oxide as an Electrocatalyst Counter Electrode in Dye-Sensitized Solar Cells</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A SnS2/graphene (SnS2/G) hybrid was synthesized by a facile 1-step solvothermal route using graphite oxide, Na sulfide, and SnCl4·5H2O as the starting materials.  The formation of SnS2 and the redn. of graphite oxide occur simultaneously.  Ultrathin SnS2 nanoplates with a lateral size of 5-10 nm are anchored on graphene nanosheets with a preferential (001) orientation, forming a unique plate-on-sheet structure.
